  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f4d30468-0377-40f3-881d-03c604a5890b'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer16072146630536971034">For Dr. David Beck, the loss was shattering. And every day for the past eight years, he has relived the horror of what happened. The gleaming lake. The pale moonlight. The piercing screams. The night his wife was taken. The last night he saw her alive.<br/><br/>Everyone tells him it's time to move on, to forget the past once and for all. But for David Beck, there can be no closure. </span>
  <span id="freeText16072146630536971034" style="display:none">For Dr. David Beck, the loss was shattering. And every day for the past eight years, he has relived the horror of what happened. The gleaming lake. The pale moonlight. The piercing screams. The night his wife was taken. The last night he saw her alive.<br /><br />Everyone tells him it's time to move on, to forget the past once and for all. But for David Beck, there can be no closure. A message has appeared on his computer, a phrase only he and his dead wife know. Suddenly Beck is taunted with the impossible- that somewhere, somehow, Elizabeth is alive.<br /><br />Beck has been warned to tell no one. And he doesn't. Instead, he runs from the people he trusts the most, plunging headlong into a search for the shadowy figure whose messages hold out a desperate hope.<br /><br />But already Beck is being hunted down. He's headed straight into the heart of a dark and deadly secret- and someone intends to stop him before he gets there.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is the best Harlan Coben book, and I have read them all. It is a mystery/thriller. While some of his books have a romance in them, wand this one <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is the best Harlan Coben book, and I have read them all. It is a mystery/thriller. While some of his books have a romance in them, wand this one does, I would never consider them a romantic suspense.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2466304452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466304452" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2466304452?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2466304452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17957866239265576256">Thank you to all the people who commented on my review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26109394.Fool_Me_Once' title='Fool Me Once by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fool Me Once</a> and told me I should have been reading this one instead - you were absolutely right!<br/><br/><b>I thought this was a great thriller</b>. The exciting premise hooked me instantly, and a combination of fast-pacing, twists, and character dynamics kept me interested until the very last page. I now see why Coben is such a well-loved writer; <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43933.Tell_No_One' title='Tell No One by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tell No One</a> is an addictive wild ride that keeps opening up more and more questions until, suddenly, it all</span>
  <span id="freeText17957866239265576256" style="display:none">Thank you to all the people who commented on my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26109394.Fool_Me_Once" title="Fool Me Once by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Fool Me Once</a> and told me I should have been reading this one instead - you were absolutely right!<br /><br /><b>I thought this was a great thriller</b>. The exciting premise hooked me instantly, and a combination of fast-pacing, twists, and character dynamics kept me interested until the very last page. I now see why Coben is such a well-loved writer; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43933.Tell_No_One" title="Tell No One by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell No One</a> is an addictive wild ride that keeps opening up more and more questions until, suddenly, it all comes together.<br /><br />I'm actually really fascinated by the mystery/thriller writing process. Especially the ones where an author can successfully pull off surprising twists without any deus ex machina. Here, Coben doesn't pull out any extraneous info at the last minute to make his mystery work. In fact, <b>he hides all his clues in plain sight</b>, so when he eventually reveals all, you realise all the pieces were there all along, and yet he had somehow managed to conceal them by the intricacy of the plot. Fabulous.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43933.Tell_No_One" title="Tell No One by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell No One</a> is the story of Dr. David Beck and his wife, Elizabeth, who was murdered eight years ago. In the present, two things happen to disturb the facade of normality David has built for himself - 1) He receives a strange email leading him to believe Elizabeth might be alive, and 2) The case is reopened by a discovery at the murder scene. Suddenly, David is forced to question again what happened all those years ago and, what's more, he may even be the lead suspect in the murder investigation.<br /><br />Old secrets come to light and, of course, the truth is so much more than anyone could have imagined!<br /><br />Having now read this, I can see how Coben has inspired other mystery/thriller writers since. I can see his influence even in Stephen King's writings, and there's especially a number of similarities between this and the new B.A. Paris book - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36448554.Bring_Me_Back" title="Bring Me Back by B.A. Paris" rel="nofollow noopener">Bring Me Back</a> - but this one was done FAR better, in my opinion.<br /><br />Anyway, I really enjoyed it. I'll happily take more Coben recommendations.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17957866239265576256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12071669282381187252">5/5 stars.<br/>Harlan Coben strikes again.<br/>This book teaches us the power of love. Sometimes I tend to believe that there is no such thing as "true love." Maybe not, maybe yes. I don't know. But what are books for? For experiencing things that you do not experience in your reality. I'm experiencing another person's reality. And in this book, the love between Beck and Elizabeth was outstanding. Despite the difficulty, despite the shit the world offers us, this little magic called "love", still remains </span>
  <span id="freeText12071669282381187252" style="display:none">5/5 stars.<br />Harlan Coben strikes again.<br />This book teaches us the power of love. Sometimes I tend to believe that there is no such thing as "true love." Maybe not, maybe yes. I don't know. But what are books for? For experiencing things that you do not experience in your reality. I'm experiencing another person's reality. And in this book, the love between Beck and Elizabeth was outstanding. Despite the difficulty, despite the shit the world offers us, this little magic called "love", still remains in the heart.<br />I admire Beck. He's not perfect, he's not the smartest, he's not the fastest, not the best. And that's what makes him human. That's what makes the plot, despite all the crap that the writers put in to make the book thrilling and exciting- realistic.<br />It does happen in life, to unlucky people, I guess. But sometimes it's easy to forget that the books, movies and TV shows we watch or read, with all the horrors and the chasing and the tension, do happen in reality.<br /> <br />Highly recommended! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5842679018085038575">OH MY LORD! Coben delivers again!! I'm always left in awe after reading one of his mysteries and this time I was thrown all over the place!<br/><br/>This is truly a spine tingling, fast paced, game changing novel. It was such a page turner that I stayed up late to finish it, I just had to know what happened!<br/><br/>This book is awesome. It begins with Beck and his wife at the lake for their anniversary. The night begins nicely for the couple until Elizabeth's scream pierces the air and Beck is attacked. When he w</span>
  <span id="freeText5842679018085038575" style="display:none">OH MY LORD! Coben delivers again!! I'm always left in awe after reading one of his mysteries and this time I was thrown all over the place!<br /><br />This is truly a spine tingling, fast paced, game changing novel. It was such a page turner that I stayed up late to finish it, I just had to know what happened!<br /><br />This book is awesome. It begins with Beck and his wife at the lake for their anniversary. The night begins nicely for the couple until Elizabeth's scream pierces the air and Beck is attacked. When he wakes he is told his wife is..... Dead.<br /><br />Eight years later Beck is at work and gets a strange email..... And from there the chase is on. Is Elizabeth dead or not? Beck goes from being a doctor to knocking down cops in the matter of one day. <br /><br />Coben has a way of pulling every single character in the book back to one event... He knows how to pull them back in like a magnet.<br /><br />I swear Coben is one of the best authors I've read. The books are thrilling, page turners and I can't get enough of them. Sometimes I have to go back and reread parts to make sure I got them right. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book. You will love it!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_791905482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791905482" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791905482?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=signed-by-author">signed-by-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=vast-conspiracy">vast-conspiracy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791905482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13833853859739278095">Dr. David Beck and his wife Elizabeth are the kind of couple that is so perfect that most of us would hate them. They met when they were little kids and they’ve been in love ever since. They’ve got cute little code phrases like ‘kiss time’ that marks their first smooch, which they know to the minute, of course. <br/><br/>So when a super happy couple like this has an anniversary to celebrate, they wouldn’t think of doing anything as pedestrian as maybe going out for a nice dinner with a couple of cocktails</span>
  <span id="freeText13833853859739278095" style="display:none">Dr. David Beck and his wife Elizabeth are the kind of couple that is so perfect that most of us would hate them. They met when they were little kids and they’ve been in love ever since. They’ve got cute little code phrases like ‘kiss time’ that marks their first smooch, which they know to the minute, of course. <br /><br />So when a super happy couple like this has an anniversary to celebrate, they wouldn’t think of doing anything as pedestrian as maybe going out for a nice dinner with a couple of cocktails and then returning home to sit on the couch in their sweat pants and watch <i>The Big Bang Theory</i>. Instead, they drive out to the lakeside cabin to the spot of their first kiss which they commemorate by reenacting the event and then marking another notch into the tree they carved their initials into the first time they swapped saliva.<br /><br />If this isn’t enough, then they go down to the lake for a little moonlight skinny dipping and bow-chick-a-bow-wow. At this point, even the marketing people who come up with those romantic commercials that try to convince people to buy blood diamonds to celebrate their love are gagging and saying, “Oh, come on! That’s too much!”<br /><br />Apparently a serial killer observed these proceedings and was so sickened by their public displays of affection that he kidnapped and killed Elizabeth after bonking David on the head. 8 years later and David is still in mourning for the lost love of his life. As the police make a grisly discovery near the scene of Elizabeth’s abduction that calls the official version of events into question, David gets a mysterious email that prompts him to an on-line video feed in which he sees something shocking. David finds himself wrapped up in a dangerous conspiracy as he tries to learn what really happened to his wife.<br /><br />This is OK as far as thrillers go. It’s got a nice hook to it, but like a lot of these types of story, the plot twists eventually take a turn into pure outlandishness. Plus, I read Coben’s newer book <i>Six Years</i> recently, and that one also involves a man trying to unravel a mystery regarding his lost love so even though this one came first, it seemed more than a little repetitive to me. <br /><br />This book works very, very hard to convince you that the two lovebirds were truly soul mates. I guess Coben has to really sell that idea so that you’d believe that anyone would risk their lives to find the truth so I get why he writes it like that. It still makes them unbelievable characters because they’re just too perfect as a couple, and that prevented me from fully buying in to the story.<br /><br />So far I prefer his Myron Bolitor series a lot more than the stand-alone thrillers of his I’ve read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13833853859739278095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17082098189873079005">I had never read anything by Harlan Coben and had heard he was a good mystery/suspense writer. I disagree. This book was horrible. I almost gave it NO stars, BUT, to my own discredit, I WAS sucked in to the plot and kind of wanted to keep reading it. However, all along, I noticed the bad writing, the improbable plot twists which never seemed to end, and the completely contrived situations to help set up those plot twists. For example, having Dr. Beck take care of and befriend a black thug drug d</span>
  <span id="freeText17082098189873079005" style="display:none">I had never read anything by Harlan Coben and had heard he was a good mystery/suspense writer. I disagree. This book was horrible. I almost gave it NO stars, BUT, to my own discredit, I WAS sucked in to the plot and kind of wanted to keep reading it. However, all along, I noticed the bad writing, the improbable plot twists which never seemed to end, and the completely contrived situations to help set up those plot twists. For example, having Dr. Beck take care of and befriend a black thug drug dealer's son only so that this same black thug could be his back up man later on? Wow, that was SO predictable and so lame. Then the whole idea of his wife's disappearance being turned on it's head just did NOT seem realistic. If they were so in love and so in tune, I just don't think it would have happened the way it did... that she'd hide all this from him. And more kept getting revealed to switch EVERYTHING around up til the very last page! It was as if Coben was paranoid that not enough excitement existed in the book so he had to keep throwing stuff at the book, everything but the kitchen sink. I will stick with the one star for suspense, but NO STARS for everything else: corny dialogue, silly plot, predictable plot.... and on and on. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17082098189873079005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3237803-sandra?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer8069195369693761924">Beck and his wife Elizabeth make their annual stop at Lake Charmaine where they carve a notch into a tree where they first kissed years ago. Later they swim in the lake and make love. Beck stays in the lake while Elizabeth swims ashore. Beck then hears a car door slam, he hears Elizabeth scream, and he sees her disappear into the semi-darkness of the night. When he quickly swims back to shore and climbs onto the dock he is hit a few times with a baseball bat and falls back into the water. He is </span>
  <span id="freeText8069195369693761924" style="display:none">Beck and his wife Elizabeth make their annual stop at Lake Charmaine where they carve a notch into a tree where they first kissed years ago. Later they swim in the lake and make love. Beck stays in the lake while Elizabeth swims ashore. Beck then hears a car door slam, he hears Elizabeth scream, and he sees her disappear into the semi-darkness of the night. When he quickly swims back to shore and climbs onto the dock he is hit a few times with a baseball bat and falls back into the water. He is told later that he supposedly came out of the water and called an ambulance for help. Elizabeth is missing and later is found dead on the side of a road days later.<br /><br />Eight years later…<br /><br />Beck is a pediatrician at a Washington Heights Clinic. One day he gets a message on his computer, a phrase only he and his wife know. A web link is attached to the email…in it he sees what appears to be Elizabeth in a webcam on a street, looking at him and saying she is sorry. She sends him another email, ending with “They’re watching. Tell no one.” Could it be possible that Elizabeth is still alive? After eight years? Beck never ID’d her body, her father did. Looking for answers Beck gets some help from his friends. But suddenly he is also being framed for the murder of Elizabeth! It seems two dead bodies of men have been discovered that were buried at Lake Charmaine, along with a baseball bat. The FBI is convinced that Beck did it. Now Beck is on the run, from the FBI and the police.<br /><br />This was a very captivating read even though I didn't like how the book ended...I found it a bit confusing. I liked Beck's friends that helped him out along the way, like Tyrese, a drug dealer from the streets. This was a fast-paced read with some really evil bad guys (Asian Wu with his killer hands) and lots of action and suspense.</span>

  <span id="freeText16379651645194035228" style="display:none">Oh no! I've just rated a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben" title="Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Harlan Coben</a> book only three stars!   <span id="freeText18311611815847420494" style="display:none">With Coben, it's very hard to review a book without mentioning spoilers. If I wrote what I want to write, my review would look like a heavily redacted top secret file. So, I will just hit on some key points:<br /><br />- Coben does it again! Very mysterious and entertaining. If you like other Coben, you will lime this. <br />- Sometimes confusing. Not to bad, just part of all the twists and turns Coben always throws in.<br />- Great characters. Not too complex, in fact they are basically caricatures, but really fun to see how they all take part in the story.<br />- Stand-alone - you can read this without reading any other Coben first. <br /><br />Summary: fun, intriguing, suspenseful, mysterious, and recommended for anyone who likes their mysteries with shocking twists and turns. </span>

  <blockquote>“The sun was now in its death throes, bruising the sky a coiling purple and orange.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478612545i/21090123.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is unbelievably awesome. First of all, I'd like to say that I had avoided reading it for too long until I had a chance to try it, then I couldn't putting it down even I had a lot of work this week. Tell No One has a straightforward narration. We believed wholeheatedly about what the author tried to tell, but after that, he revealed a distrustful evidence making us reconsider our thought again and again till the end. And this is what makes the book so special for me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478573254ra/21085488.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Memories, you see, hurt. The good ones most of all.”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>I enjoyed Harlan Coben's writing style so much. He surprsied me with many twists, and the whole plot was thoroughly planned. In my opinion, I do think that Tell No One is the best crime book I've ever read since I last picked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9736930.Before_I_Go_to_Sleep" title="Before I Go to Sleep by S.J. Watson" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Go to Sleep</a> in 2014. Coben successfully stuck me with the emotion that left me wanting to read crime novels again this year. And now I'm irrevocably a fan of him !<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Don't show me paradise and then burn it down”</blockquote>
</b> <br><br>David Beck is a multidimensional character even though he presented the flat one for the first few chapters. After he digs into the evidences of his wife and is aware that maybe she's still alive, the book leaps to the highest tempo because of his mind and my suspicion that craving some answers, and you have no idea how much that feeling hit my brain so many times until I promised my self I had to finish this book before midnight. Tell No One also has thrilling vibes and action scens, too, so you don't have to worry that it will bore you to death.<br><br>After I finished Tell No One, I have to tell EVERYONE about how amazing this book is. Harlen Coben will be the first author, from now on, when I think of crime novels, I'll pick his other books without hesitation.<br><br>4.5 stars for this mind-blowing and cunning book ! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478612545i/21090124._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thai review : <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/ddz2jc">https://goo.gl/ddz2jc</a></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307491732" href="/book/show/7084510-tell-no-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer593736991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11832391029985614718">I’m a fan of Harlan Coben’s Myron Bolitar series and decided that I’d start this book without reading the synopsis. It was selected as the book for group discussion in one of my groups and was highly touted. The book was that much more exciting because I didn’t know what it was about and read the prologue with no clue as to where it was going. Here’s what I’ll say about it so you can have a similar experience if you choose. <br/><br/>I had a really tough time putting this book down for interruptions (slee</span>
  <span id="freeText11832391029985614718" style="display:none">I’m a fan of Harlan Coben’s Myron Bolitar series and decided that I’d start this book without reading the synopsis. It was selected as the book for group discussion in one of my groups and was highly touted. The book was that much more exciting because I didn’t know what it was about and read the prologue with no clue as to where it was going. Here’s what I’ll say about it so you can have a similar experience if you choose. <br /><br />I had a really tough time putting this book down for interruptions (sleep, errands, meals, etc.) because it was pretty unpredictable, a staple of Coben’s stories. You think you know who the good guys are, only to be disappointed at a later juncture. Even the good guys are presented with moral dilemmas where they make dicey choices and you question your own self as to whether you would have done things differently. Here you have a man who's done nothing but the right things expected of him and in the space of 24 hours is consorting with people and doing things he would never have considered as an option the day before.<br /><br />The story kept me off balance the entire time and the twist at the end really caught me off guard, just when I believed I had everything sorted out. If you like tension, action, mystery and strange suspense and a little bit of romance, you’ll like this book. I certainly did. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11832391029985614718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2005929612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2005929612" />
    <a title="Sumit RK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38271102-sumit-rk"><img alt="Sumit RK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599896274p2/38271102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005929612?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sumit RK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sumit RK" href="/user/show/38271102-sumit-rk">Sumit RK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2005929612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16568494200310599493">As a mystery thriller,<i>Tell No One</i> delivers nonstop from start to the end. Right from the impactful start, there is never a dull moment in the story. The protagonist, Beck and the rest of characters (along with a string of bad guys) are mostly well written. Coben keeps the story fast paced while introducing new twists & turns at regular intervals that keeps you hooked right till the end (like a good thriller should). <br/> <br/> What I really didn’t like was the climax. During the long winded final act, th</span>
  <span id="freeText16568494200310599493" style="display:none">As a mystery thriller,<i>Tell No One</i> delivers nonstop from start to the end. Right from the impactful start, there is never a dull moment in the story. The protagonist, Beck and the rest of characters (along with a string of bad guys) are mostly well written. Coben keeps the story fast paced while introducing new twists &amp; turns at regular intervals that keeps you hooked right till the end (like a good thriller should). <br /> <br /> What I really didn’t like was the climax. During the long winded final act, the story introduces a series of twists and turns, which almost ruins the entire story for you. Especially the final twist is so convoluted, that the entire story doesn’t make sense, if you try putting it together backwards. <br /><br /> In summary, Apart from the flaws, Tell No One is good read &amp; it will keep you entertained. If you like twists and turns,unlikely heroes and page turning action, you will enjoy this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16568494200310599493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText804975538036430662" style="display:none">Tell No One, Harlan Coben<br />Tell No One is a thriller novel by American writer Harlan Coben, published in 2001. For Dr. David Beck, the loss was shattering. And every day for the past eight years, he has relived the horror of what happened. The gleaming lake. The pale moonlight. The piercing screams. The night his wife was taken. The last night he saw her alive. Everyone tells him it's time to move on, to forget the past once and for all. But for David Beck, there can be no closure. A message has appeared on his computer, a phrase only he and his dead wife know. Suddenly Beck is taunted with the impossible- that somewhere, somehow, Elizabeth is alive. Beck has been warned to tell no one. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه نوامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br />عنوان: به هیچ کس نگو؛ نویسنده: هرلن (هارلن) كوبن؛ بهزاد رحمتی؛ تهران : چلچله، ‏‫1396؛ در 481 ص؛ شابک: 9786008625551؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران: کتابسرای میردشتی، ‏‫1397؛ در 424 ص؛ شابک: 9786229504123؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان ایالات متحده آمریکا - سده 21 م<br />‬<br />کتاب «به هیچ کس نگو» اثری از «هارلن کوبن»، نویسنده ی آمریکایی است، که نخستین بار در سال 2001 میلادی منتشر و موفق به کسب جایزه «ادگار» شد؛ در بسیاری از رمانهای ایشان بازگویی رخدادهای حل نشده ی گذشته، و حادثه های منجر به مرگ است، و ویژگی بارز آثارش پیچشهای ناگهانی در داستان، و شوکه کردن خوانشگر است. درد فقدان برای دکتر «دیوید بک»، کمرشکن بود. و او هر روز، در طول هشت سال بگذشته، با ترس و وحشت آن اتفاق را، زندگی کرده است. آن برکه ی درخشان. نور کمسوی ماه. شیونهای دلخراش. همان شبی که همسرش را ربودند. همان شبی که آخرین بار او را زنده دید. همه به «دیوید» میگویند که وقت گذشتن از آن ماجرا و فراموش کردن گذشته، یک بار برای همیشه، فرا رسیده است. اما برای «دیوید بک»، پایانی در کار نخواهد بود. پیامی بر صفحه ی کامپیوتر او ظاهر شده، که حاوی عبارتی است که فقط او و همسرش میدانستند. «دیوید بک» ناگهان با غیرممکنها روبرو شده است؛ اینکه در جایی، و به طریقی، «الیزابت» هنوز زنده است. ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7148977499464387832">I would like to know - <b>Are all Coben's books this good??!</b><br/><br/>Tell No One was right up my street. I loved everything about this page turner - the characters, the clever plot, the twists... I call that AWESOMENESS!<br/><br/>I listened to the audio book and normally, I only listen to audiobooks when running or walking. With this one, I just couldn't stop (no, I didn't do more running), but I listened to it at home, which only shows how much I enjoyed it.   <span id="freeText7148977499464387832" style="display:none">I would like to know - <b>Are all Coben's books this good??!</b><br /><br />Tell No One was right up my street. I loved everything about this page turner - the characters, the clever plot, the twists... I call that AWESOMENESS!<br /><br />I listened to the audio book and normally, I only listen to audiobooks when running or walking. With this one, I just couldn't stop (no, I didn't do more running), but I listened to it at home, which only shows how much I enjoyed it. The narrator did a great job, making my audio experience very atmospheric.<br /><br />I think the last time I got this excited about a crime novel was when I read <i>The Dry by Harper</i>. I am now off to order a few copies of the book and give them to my friends and family! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11889840929463986390">Dr. David Beck receives mysterious emails eight years after his long time childhood friend, and wife for six months was taken. The 13th ring around a heart with their names in against the tree, was the last time they would celebrate a love that started out just about their first year together in school. It was impossible for him to get over the events and move on with his life. <br/><br/>He had no other choice but to sleuth his way to the truth of what happened that night in the lake when Elizabeth disapp</span>
  <span id="freeText11889840929463986390" style="display:none">Dr. David Beck receives mysterious emails eight years after his long time childhood friend, and wife for six months was taken. The 13th ring around a heart with their names in against the tree, was the last time they would celebrate a love that started out just about their first year together in school. It was impossible for him to get over the events and move on with his life. <br /><br />He had no other choice but to sleuth his way to the truth of what happened that night in the lake when Elizabeth disappeared and he woke up in the hospital five days later.<br /><br />Now, after all these years he was warned not to tell anyone about the emails. And he didn't. And the clues keep stacking up that there was much more to his memories than the serial killer who was arrested for a crime. Someone was sending him pieces of his own memories he had never shared with anyone ... <br /><br />In an unpredictable, fast-moving suspense drama, the past is connecting with the present at breakneck speed. Nothing seemed what is was, and people had a side to them he had yet to discover. <br /><br />A really good read!</span>

<div id="review_3316839890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3316839890" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3316839890?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/39724184-tell-no-one">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=definitely-not-young-adult">definitely-not-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3316839890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16917319547715088900">My second <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben' title='Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harlan Coben</a> novel and sure enough, I wasn't disappointed. It was fast paced, gripping, and entertaining. That's what I really enjoy in his books, how they're written intensely and at the same time wittily. The humor always gets me and I always admire such a skill from an author, when they could make you laugh while under pressure. Lol.<br/><br/>Admittedly, I find the plot pretty formulaic because I find quite a lot of similarities with that of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15811568.Six_Years' title='Six Years by Harlan Coben' rel='nofollow noopener'>Six Years</a>. Professional and upstanding guy suddenly</span>
  <span id="freeText16917319547715088900" style="display:none">My second <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben" title="Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Harlan Coben</a> novel and sure enough, I wasn't disappointed. It was fast paced, gripping, and entertaining. That's what I really enjoy in his books, how they're written intensely and at the same time wittily. The humor always gets me and I always admire such a skill from an author, when they could make you laugh while under pressure. Lol.<br /><br />Admittedly, I find the plot pretty formulaic because I find quite a lot of similarities with that of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15811568.Six_Years" title="Six Years by Harlan Coben" rel="nofollow noopener">Six Years</a>. Professional and upstanding guy suddenly finds himself in an impossible dilemma with both the authorities and the bad guys  and yet I still completely bought it. <br /><br />That's the magic of wonderful writing, which may I say reads very current. If not for Dr. Beck's beeper, I wouldn't have thought the book was first published in 2001. And of course, let's not forget to add the short chapters which I'm a huge fan of and the cheesy romance because that seems one of the things that make Coben's books even more enjoyable. Lol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16917319547715088900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15156956482081269668">There are page turners and there are page turners with cherries on top. This has a cherry on top.<br/>Eight years ago Dr. David Beck is devastated when his lovely young wife is abducted and then murdered.   <span id="freeText15156956482081269668" style="display:none">There are page turners and there are page turners with cherries on top. This has a cherry on top.<br />Eight years ago Dr. David Beck is devastated when his lovely young wife is abducted and then murdered. Eight years on David still has not come to terms with his lose but is getting by the best he can. Out of know where he gets a cryptic email with information that only his wife could know. He logs on and gets the shock of his life when he sees a live stream with his dead wife, who looks very much alive, in it.<br />At the same time, eight years ago, a young man is shot and killed. The young man's father, a billionaire with all the reach that that kind of money can bring, is also devastated at his lose. The father believes that David's wife was responsible for his son's death. The father never sure that David's wife is really dead has kept tabs on David for the last eight years. David's house is bugged so when David gets the email from his dead wife the bereaved father leaves no stone unturned to learn the truth.<br /><br />What happens next is a will deprive you of sleep and the book will become a permanent extension of your hand until the last page.<br /><br />This is a high octane thriller that will have your nails bitten to the quick.<br />Highly recommended.</span>

  <span id="freeText5509383940915917877" style="display:none">For Dr. David Beck, the loss was shattering. And every day for the past eight years, he has relived the horror of what happened. Everyone tells him it's time to move on, to forget the past once and for all. But for David Beck, there can be no closure. First few pages sucked me right into the plot- what happened that night! <br/><br/>Its about a grieving husband Dr.Beck whose wife was brutally murdered 8 years ago. But, then strange things start happening one after the other which makes him question everything that happened on that fateful night . <br/><br/>Story is fast paced and very addictive.   <span id="freeText4942703913808574213" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5 ⭐</b><br><br>The story started off pretty well. The first 3/4th or so gets a big big 👍 . First few pages sucked me right into the plot- what happened that night! <br><br>Its about a grieving husband Dr.Beck whose wife was brutally murdered 8 years ago. But, then strange things start happening one after the other which makes him question everything that happened on that fateful night . <br><br>Story is fast paced and very addictive. I enjoyed the writing style which is direct and to the point. Its always a very good sign if the reader is still scratching head at 60% - what the hell happened that night ? I think the problem for me was that my expectations got too high so the final act just felt okayish to me –a little too Bollywoody 😬 . <br><br>Yes,the author did a nice job of neatly tying up all loose ends .And yes there are many twists and turns …too many. The first twist I was like…whoa wow<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1532935673ra/26049268.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But the author threw in one more..and then there were more ..to the point that the last one felt a bit like <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1502615804ra/23576084.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were some cliché emotional drama that unnecessarily dragged the last bit. And also I had trouble accepting author’s reasoning as to why things happened the way it did.<br><br>In short, a good read that could have been great .My very first Harlan Coben book …not going to be my last .Though I do feel the story read more like a movie script. So watching the movie might be a better option😉.</span>

<div id="review_2473059688" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2473059688" />
    <a title="Alice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67934812-alice"><img alt="Alice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517307666p2/67934812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2473059688?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice" href="/user/show/67934812-alice">Alice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67934812-alice?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2473059688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9297959332953918481">3.5* DON'T READ THE COMMENTS IF YOU DON'T WANT TO BE SPOILED. ALSO I ACTUALLY LIKE THIS BOOK I JUST DON'T LOVE IT.<br/>Seriously fuck this book it's so convoluted. Just read my spoiler section that took 2 hours to write because I was trying to figure out how the plot points connected. This isn't the type of mystery that you the reader is trying to figure out it's more going along with mystery as the characters are finding out. I really like some of the side characters like Tyrese' Eric, Shauna, and t</span>
  <span id="freeText9297959332953918481" style="display:none">3.5* DON'T READ THE COMMENTS IF YOU DON'T WANT TO BE SPOILED. ALSO I ACTUALLY LIKE THIS BOOK I JUST DON'T LOVE IT.<br />Seriously fuck this book it's so convoluted. Just read my spoiler section that took 2 hours to write because I was trying to figure out how the plot points connected. This isn't the type of mystery that you the reader is trying to figure out it's more going along with mystery as the characters are finding out. I really like some of the side characters like Tyrese' Eric, Shauna, and that one police guy. Beck himself is just ok which is kinda lame. Something about this book I feel like it needed more heart. I don't really know what that means, but it was missing that spark for me in a lot of things. Like the characters could have been even better, could have been more fun, the mystery could have been more compelling. I think it's because it jumped between lot's of perspectives or maybe because it's never had a shit got weird moment. Like it got crazy, but it could have been crazier and weirder.<br /><br />There was too much going on. I'll be surprised if anyone could completely and accurately explain how each reveal was connected in the mystery. So I read this because of Emily May's review and while I agree it doesn't pull anything completely unknown some of the reasoning for what happened I didn't really like. There were definitely some things you couldn't have guessed out with out it being revealed to you which is why the mystery portion wasn't that fun for me because besides basic predictions about who is bad I didn't really have any guesses for what was coming next.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (David Beck and Elizabeth are married) (Griffin Scope is the bad guy who are after Beck and Elizabeth for the death of his son Brandon Scope) (literally everyone calls David (Dr. Beck) so I'm going to refer to him after Beck)<br /><br />I'm not so sure about the ending, but what really happened is that Beck's dad found out Brandon Scope was bad after working with him and told Elizabeth's father (Hoyt), but Hoyt was working with Griffin Scope at the time and told Griffin about Beck's dad because he didn't think that Griffin would murder Beck's dad for his suspicion of his son Brandon Scope. So Griffin Scope murdered Beck's dad because of Elizabeth's father Hoyt revealing information to the Scopes.<br /><br />In the story Elizabeth worked with Brandon Scope in charity work. So when Brandon Scope was still alive he went after Beck with a knife after breaking into Beck's and Elizabeth's home. (because of Beck's father? or because Elizabeth knew he was bad, probably because Elizabeth knew he was bad). So was Brandon going after Elizabeth when he broke into their house, but Beck happened to be the one in the house so they fought and Beck is the one that ended up killing him in self defense. So Elizabeth knew this and hid the evidence so the super powerful Griffin Scope wouldn't come after Beck.<br /><br />So Elizabeth and Beck's dad were conveniently both connected in knowing about how Brandon Scope was evil, but it got complicated because Elizabeth's father Hoyt who is a police officer was collaborating with Scope and accidentally got Beck's father murdered by Scope. <br /><br />Here's the thing. This whole time Hoyt thinks Elizabeth really is the one who killed Brandon Scope because she's covering for Beck. All the bad guys with Scope also think Elizabeth did it because she covered for some guy who her father Hoyt was trying to blame the murder of Brandon on. So the two hitmen that tried to kill Elizabeth bodies are found (Hoyt killed them because he didn't trust them to stay quiet about Elizabeth who they didn't actually attack because Elizabeth is alive and there is a fake body) (Beck got attacked still because Hoyt didn't care what happened to him) so the bad guys now are pretty sure Elizabeth is still alive because the 2 hitmen were in supposed to be out of the country from what the 2 guys told Griffin Scope. So the bad guys are following Beck (to find Elizabeth I think? because she is contacting him in code) and they end up almost framing him for the murder of the 2 guys and Elizabeth's best friend. So that's why Beck is on the run with his drug dealer friend Tyrese while Elizabeth is trying to contact him, but then she realizes that her coming back had caused a lot of problems for Beck and other people she knows. I don't remember why she tries to contact Beck when those bodies are found and she realizes the bad guys know she is still alive. (I know someone might say it's because Beck actually killed him, but the way it was presented did not seem like that was the reason. The whole Beck is the killer is actually just a twist at the end.)<br /><br />I still don't entirely understand all the plot points this story is so convoluted because of the title "tell no one" several characters are lying about what they did and it gets revealed later on, but by that point I already forgot several other details so I'm not why certain events are connected. Apparently the police being after Beck isn't really connected to the bad guys(Scope) hunting him down it's just a side of the bad guys tying to frame him for killing Elizabeth and get him on the run.<br /><br />So the "tell no one" aspects are:<br />Elizabeth hiding that Beck killed Brandon Scope.<br /><br />Beck's sister Lisa hiding the fact that she knows Brandon Scope beat Elizabeth and took pictures as proof. (Stupidest plot point by the way Elizabeth telling her to not tell anyone after all that happened is a horrible reason for Lisa to tell NO ONE at all) and then she ended up telling anyway which finally alerted the other character on the Scopes involvement in all this. So fucking stupid.<br /><br />Beck hiding until the end of the story that he's really the one who killed Brandon Scope in self defense.<br /><br />Elizabeth's father Hoyt having to create the fake murder of Elizabeth to help her go into hiding because she told him she (instead of Beck) killed Brandon Scope in self defense.<br />Hoyt also hiding from Beck that he got his father killed. He also got a tip that Elizabeth was going to get attacked from one of Scope's people at a certain time and place from one of the collaborators in Beck's father murder which is how Beck found out about Hoyt involvement in the death of his father. So Elizabeth made herself look sketchy because she absolved the guy that was going to be the fall guy that Hoyt set up for the murder of Brandon Scope. So now the bad guys think she did it and Hoyt also thinks she did it because of what she told him covering for Beck. Luckily Hoyt was tipped off for her attempted murder by one of Scope's hitmen who murdered Beck's father (just because he wanted more money) so the murder was faked and she got out of the country. Hoyt killed the hitmen anyway because he didn't trust them and then their bodies were found 8 years later and that's how Beck gets involved and almost gets framed for the murder of everyone<br /><br />This is why I'm fucking confused so the whole thing about Beck's father knowing that Brandon Scope is bad is actually related to Elizabeth working with Brandon scope and also knowing he's bad it's just that they are both involved so Beck's father's murder is just so Hoyt is related to know about Elizabeth's attack.<br /><br />If any of my ponderings are wrong fuck this book because it's honestly too convoluted and I don't trust anyone who says they love the book and understand exactly what happened to connect all the events. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="9297959332953918481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15768541806198469542">One star as I managed to finish this.<br/><br/>Coben's books seem popular, so I thought I'd give it a try, in the never ending search for nice thrillers and detectives....<br/><br/>Dr David Beck tries to figure out what happened 8 years ago, when his wife and love from his childhood was killed. Or was she..?<br/><br/>I read it to the end, but at some point there came a strong feeling of BS. Now let me try to get a few hiccups why:<br/>* computer surveillance. This was supposedly happening with dial-up and in 2001 or earlier. So n</span>
  <span id="freeText15768541806198469542" style="display:none">One star as I managed to finish this.<br /><br />Coben's books seem popular, so I thought I'd give it a try, in the never ending search for nice thrillers and detectives....<br /><br />Dr David Beck tries to figure out what happened 8 years ago, when his wife and love from his childhood was killed. Or was she..?<br /><br />I read it to the end, but at some point there came a strong feeling of BS. Now let me try to get a few hiccups why:<br />* computer surveillance. This was supposedly happening with dial-up and in 2001 or earlier. So not possible in the extent they describe<br />* credibility of the whole story: screams B movie, or a B cartoon. Not a triller - thriller is supposed to thrill (in the cover it says it's a thriller) (oh wait, I've seen some trailers, so looks like they are making it a Hollywood budget movie. The story is still B so even hiring the most expensive actors can't save the story)<br />* the villains are painted way too villains. Fine for cartoons, not for a thriller<br />* solution was weaker than a homeopathic liquid diluted 1 part to 100000 of water. Who killed B.. the saint is low<br />* the painted saintness of Elizabeth, the dead-or-not wife was too icky<br />* the actions of Beck were screaming B movie in many occasions.<br /><br />Recommend no one.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookcrossing.com/journal/7658662/">http://www.bookcrossing.com/journal/7...</a><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bUCEWJC2ymJSO7ZH2FNWklHcsAwZWNzEnwogq4QlVbDNDj3YK+jJIGAhsUfIMSNgQDkc8h9SQb06CQBPFQYhUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PMQgoHmY8c3oOGkBBX6U75JXxfo4HRFsGnDI16rBDg6cipkgwsbyj9oibgEVHOEdg7JpBD4XjBW/c+gzO+J67A==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer18108044306766447920">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br/><br/>Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first aut</span>
  <span id="freeText18108044306766447920" style="display:none">With over 60 million books in print worldwide, Harlan Coben’s last seven consecutive novels, MISSING YOU, SIX YEARS, STAY CLOSE, LIVE WIRE, CAUGHT, LONG LOST and HOLD TIGHT all debuted at #1 on the <i>New York Times</i> bestseller list and lists around the world. His books are published in 43 languages around the globe.<br /><br />Coben is the winner of the Edgar Award, Shamus Award and Anthony Award – the first author to win all three – and he has received an eclectic variety of honors from all over the world. His novel TELL NO ONE has been turned into a hit French film of the same name. His essays and columns have appeared in many top publications. <br /><br />Harlan was born in Newark, New Jersey. He still lives in New Jersey with his wife, Anne Armstrong-Coben MD, a pediatrician, and their four children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18108044306766447920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
